	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Wilfred Rhodes</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<p><b>Wilfred Rhodes</b> (29 October 1877&#160;– 8 July 1973) was an English professional <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricketer</a> who played 58 <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test matches</a> for <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a> between 1899 and 1930. In Tests, Rhodes took 127 <a href="/wiki/Wicket#Dismissing_a_batsman" title="Wicket">wickets</a> and scored 2,325 <a href="/wiki/Run_(cricket)" title="Run (cricket)">runs</a>, becoming the first Englishman to complete the double of 1,000 runs and 100 wickets in Test matches. He holds the world records both for the most appearances made in <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class cricket</a> (1,110 matches), and for the most wickets taken (4,204). He completed the <a href="/wiki/Double_(cricket)" title="Double (cricket)">double</a> of 1,000 runs and 100 wickets in an English cricket season a record 16 times. Rhodes played for <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire</a> and England into his fifties, and in his final Test in 1930 was, at 52 years and 165 days, the oldest player who has appeared in a Test match.
</p><p>Beginning his career for Yorkshire in 1898 as a <a href="/wiki/Left-arm_orthodox_spin" title="Left-arm orthodox spin">slow left arm bowler</a> who was a useful batsman, Rhodes quickly established a reputation as one of the best slow bowlers in the world. However, by the First World War he had developed  his batting skills to the extent that he was regarded as one of the leading batsmen in England and had established an effective <a href="/wiki/Batting_order_(cricket)#Opening_batsmen_or_openers" title="Batting order (cricket)">opening partnership</a> with <a href="/wiki/Jack_Hobbs" title="Jack Hobbs">Jack Hobbs</a>. The improvement in Rhodes's batting was accompanied by a temporary decline in his bowling performances, but the loss of key Yorkshire bowlers after the war led to Rhodes resuming his role as a front-line bowler. He played throughout the 1920s as an <a href="/wiki/All-rounder" title="All-rounder">all-rounder</a> before retiring after the 1930 cricket season. His first appearance for England was in 1899 and he played regularly in Tests until 1921. Recalled to the team in the final <a href="/wiki/The_Ashes" title="The Ashes">Ashes</a> Test of 1926 aged 48, Rhodes played a significant part in winning the match for England who thus regained the Ashes for the first time since 1912. He ended his Test career in the West Indies in April 1930.
</p><p>As a bowler, Rhodes was noted for his great accuracy, variations in flight and, in his early days, sharp spin. Throughout his career he was particularly effective on <a href="/wiki/Sticky_wicket" title="Sticky wicket">wet, rain affected pitches</a> where he could bowl sides out for very low scores. His batting was regarded as solid and dependable but unspectacular, and critics accused him of excessive caution at times. However, they considered him to be an  astute cricket thinker. Following his retirement from playing cricket, he coached at <a href="/wiki/Harrow_School" title="Harrow School">Harrow School</a> but was not a great success. His eyesight began to fail from around 1939 to the point where he was completely blind by 1952. He was given honorary membership of the <a href="/wiki/Marylebone_Cricket_Club" title="Marylebone Cricket Club">Marylebone Cricket Club</a> (MCC) in 1949 and remained a respected figure within the game until his death in 1973. On 9 August 2009, Rhodes was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Cricket_Hall_of_Fame" title="ICC Cricket Hall of Fame">ICC Cricket Hall of Fame</a>.
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Career_after_the_First_World_War"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Career after the First World War</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Leading_bowler_again"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Leading bowler again</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Australian_tour,_1920–21"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Australian tour, 1920–21</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Senior_professional"><span class="tocnumber">3.3</span> <span class="toctext">Senior professional</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Recalled_for_the_Oval"><span class="tocnumber">3.4</span> <span class="toctext">Recalled for the Oval</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Late_career"><span class="tocnumber">3.5</span> <span class="toctext">Late career</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Retirement_and_coaching"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">Retirement and coaching</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Style_and_personality"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Style and personality</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a></li>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_career">Early life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings">Beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rhodes  was born in the village of <a href="/wiki/Kirkheaton" title="Kirkheaton">Kirkheaton</a>, just outside <a href="/wiki/Huddersfield" title="Huddersfield">Huddersfield</a>, in 1877. His family moved to a farm two miles away while he was very young.<sup id="cite_ref-Rogerson_31_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogerson_31-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> He went to school in nearby Hopton, and later to Spring Grove School in Huddersfield. His father, Alfred Rhodes, was captain of the Kirkheaton cricket team's Second XI and encouraged his son to play cricket, buying him equipment and having a pitch laid near their home for Wilfred to practice.<sup id="cite_ref-Rogerson_31_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogerson_31-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
By the time Rhodes left school, aged 16, he had joined Kirkheaton Cricket Club and started to take cricket seriously: he watched <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Yorkshire County Cricket Club">Yorkshire</a> when they played close to his home and began to consider a career as a professional cricketer. Around 1893 he took a job working on the railway in the local town of <a href="/wiki/Mirfield" title="Mirfield">Mirfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> By now playing regularly for Kirkheaton Second XI, Rhodes's keenness to reach one game on time led him to ring the off-duty bell before the end of the shift and as a result he lost his job. Subsequently, he worked on a local farm, which allowed him more time for cricket. By 1895 he achieved a place in the Kirkheaton first team, and was recommended to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gala_Cricket_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gala Cricket Club (page does not exist)">Gala Cricket Club</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Galashiels" title="Galashiels">Galashiels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, as a professional.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_club_cricketer">Professional club cricketer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Professional club cricketer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rhodes played for Gala Cricket Club in 1896 and 1897, as an all-rounder who opened the batting and bowled medium paced <a href="/wiki/Seam_bowling" title="Seam bowling">seamers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He took 92 wickets in his first season, and discovered that bowling an occasional slow ball brought him some success. He decided to change his bowling style to spin, and spent the winter of 1896–97 practising on the family farm while also working again on the railway, this time as a <a href="/wiki/Signalman_(rail)" title="Signalman (rail)">signalman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Over several months, Rhodes used his practice sessions to develop control of spin and different types of delivery. Consequently, in his second season at Galashiels, now bowling <a href="/wiki/Left-arm_orthodox_spin" title="Left-arm orthodox spin">slow left-arm</a>, he took fewer wickets but at a better average. At the end of the 1897 season, encouraged by a Scottish member of the MCC, he resigned from Gala to look for work in England.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First-class_cricketer">First-class cricketer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: First-class cricketer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginning_as_a_bowler">Beginning as a bowler</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Beginning as a bowler">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lot0622.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A cricketer about to bowl" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/Lot0622.jpg/220px-Lot0622.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/Lot0622.jpg/330px-Lot0622.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/54/Lot0622.jpg/440px-Lot0622.jpg 2x" data-file-width="582" data-file-height="798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lot0622.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wilfred Rhodes early in his career, around 1900</div></div></div>
<p>In response to an advertisement, Rhodes applied to join the groundstaff of <a href="/wiki/Warwickshire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Warwickshire County Cricket Club">Warwickshire County Cricket Club</a>, but the club were unable to offer him an engagement for financial reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> At this time, Yorkshire were looking for a slow left arm spinner to replace <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Peel" title="Bobby Peel">Bobby Peel</a>, who had been sacked following a disciplinary lapse on the field in front of his captain <a href="/wiki/Martin_Hawke,_7th_Baron_Hawke" title="Martin Hawke, 7th Baron Hawke">Lord Hawke</a> in August 1897. Rhodes successfully applied for a place in a Yorkshire Colts team to play against the County XI.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> However, by his own later admission, Rhodes had a poor match, while his rival for Peel's place in the side, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Cordingley" title="Albert Cordingley">Albert Cordingley</a>, took nine wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early spring 1898, Rhodes was invited to the nets at <a href="/wiki/Headingley_Cricket_Ground" title="Headingley Cricket Ground">Headingley</a>, which led to him playing in some friendly matches (unofficial matches involving first-class teams). Rhodes went on to make his first-class debut for Yorkshire on 12 May 1898 against the MCC, taking six wickets in the match.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In his second game, he made his <a href="/wiki/County_Championship" title="County Championship">County Championship</a> debut on 16 May 1898 against Somerset, taking 13 wickets for 45 runs.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In the 1898 season, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Wisden_Cricketers%27_Almanack" title="Wisden Cricketers&#39; Almanack">Wisden Cricketers' Almanack</a></i> Rhodes "sprang at once into fame, bowling in match after match for Yorkshire with astounding success."<sup id="cite_ref-cricketerofyear_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricketerofyear-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the season he had taken 154 wickets at an average of 14.60,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and was named as one of the <a href="/wiki/Wisden_Cricketers_of_the_Year" title="Wisden Cricketers of the Year"><i>Wisden</i> Cricketers of the Year</a> for 1899. The citation stated: "There can be no doubt as to the greatness of his achievements last summer&#160;... His qualities as a slow bowler struck everyone as being exceptional"; however,  it was noted that bad weather in first part of the summer created some difficult pitches for batting.<sup id="cite_ref-cricketerofyear_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricketerofyear-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> As a batsman he scored three fifties,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Wisden</i> rated him "a dangerous run-getter".<sup id="cite_ref-cricketerofyear_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cricketerofyear-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the season, according to cricket writer <a href="/wiki/Neville_Cardus" title="Neville Cardus">Neville Cardus</a>, Rhodes had proven himself to be the best left-arm spinner in England.<sup id="cite_ref-obituary_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1899_English_cricket_season" title="1899 English cricket season">1899</a>, Rhodes took 179 wickets at an average of 17.10 in a reasonably dry season; this weather meant that pitches were harder, easier to bat on, and less likely to suit his bowling. <i>Wisden</i> described him as "head and shoulders above his colleagues".<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-R54_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R54-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> He made his Test debut in <a href="/wiki/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1899" title="Australian cricket team in England in 1899">the five-match series against Australia</a>, playing in three of the five Tests; his first Test coincided with <a href="/wiki/W._G._Grace" title="W. G. Grace">W. G. Grace</a>'s last. As well as Grace, his teammates included <a href="/wiki/C._B._Fry" title="C. B. Fry">C. B. Fry</a>, <a href="/wiki/K._S._Ranjitsinhji" class="mw-redirect" title="K. S. Ranjitsinhji">K. S. Ranjitsinhji</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_Hirst" title="George Hirst">George Hirst</a>. Rhodes opened the English bowling and took four wickets for 58 in an Australian total of 252; his first Test wicket was <a href="/wiki/Monty_Noble" title="Monty Noble">Monty Noble</a> (whose wicket he took again in the second innings). He was described by <i>Wisden</i> as bowling "steady and well" on the first day.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes took three wickets in the second Test,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> but the selectors omitted him from the third match, a decision <i>Wisden</i> believed was mistaken.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He did not play again until the final Test, and he finished with 13 wickets in the series, equal with <a href="/wiki/J._T._Hearne" title="J. T. Hearne">J. T. Hearne</a> as England's leading Test wicket-taker for the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes was also selected to represent <a href="/wiki/Gentlemen_v_Players" title="Gentlemen v Players">the Players against the Gentlemen</a> at Lord's for the first time that season, although W. G. Grace and C. B. Fry scored heavily against him.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rhodes's most successful seasons in terms of wickets were the three seasons from 1900 to 1902. In these years, Rhodes took 725 wickets at an average of 14.07, taking five or more wickets in an innings 68 times and taking ten or more wickets in a match 21 times,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> assisting Yorkshire to three consecutive <a href="/wiki/County_Championship" title="County Championship">County Championships</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1900_English_cricket_season" title="1900 English cricket season">1900</a>, Rhodes took 261 wickets as bad weather made pitches helpful to his bowling. In <a href="/wiki/1901_English_cricket_season" title="1901 English cricket season">1901</a>, the weather was much better, leading to pitches that were good for batting, but Rhodes took 251 wickets, an achievement described by <i>Wisden</i> as astonishing.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rogerson,_p._62_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogerson,_p._62-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Against MCC that year, Rhodes scored his maiden first-class century, batting at number nine.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/1902_English_cricket_season" title="1902 English cricket season">the 1902 season</a>, Rhodes took 213 wickets, fewer than 1901 despite a greater number of favourable pitches in a wet summer. This attracted unfavourable comment from some critics who had expected more.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main cricket event of 1902 was the <a href="/wiki/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1902" title="Australian cricket team in England in 1902">Australian tour of England</a>. Rhodes played in all five Tests and was England's leading wicket-taker with 22 wickets at an average of 15.27.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He took seven for 17 in the first innings of the first Test, out of an Australian total of 36, in conditions that the umpires considered reasonable for batting; <i>Wisden</i> noted that Rhodes and Hirst bowled very well.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> However, C. B. Fry believed that Hirst was more difficult to play and that while Rhodes bowled well, the Australian batsmen got themselves out as they "hurried to the other end and tried to hit Rhodes, without success".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Rain meant the game was drawn and washed out most of the second match. In the third Test, which England lost, Rhodes took five for 63,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> including a spell of four wickets in nineteen balls.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In the fourth Test, Rhodes took seven wickets in the match, taking three quick wickets in the first innings, but receiving some heavy punishment. He was batting at the end of the match, but was unable to prevent Australia from snatching victory to win by three runs and take the series.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The final Test, at <a href="/wiki/The_Oval" title="The Oval">The Oval</a>, was dominated by <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Jessop" title="Gilbert Jessop">Gilbert Jessop</a> and Hirst, but when England needed 263 to win in the final innings, Rhodes came into bat after the ninth wicket fell with 15 needed for England to win. It has been claimed that Hirst said to Rhodes, "We'll get 'em in singles",<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> but neither batsman could remember those words being said and not all the runs came in singles.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The two Yorkshiremen were not dismissed and England won by one wicket.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1903_English_cricket_season" title="1903 English cricket season">1903</a>, Rhodes scored over 1,000 runs in the season for the first time,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> in the process completing his first <a href="/wiki/Double_(cricket)" title="Double (cricket)">double</a> of 1,000 runs and 100 wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However, after bowling a large number of overs against <a href="/wiki/Worcestershire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Worcestershire County Cricket Club">Worcestershire</a> early in the season, he had little success as a bowler for a spell of three weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pelham_Warner" title="Pelham Warner">Pelham Warner</a>, a leading <a href="/wiki/Amateur_status_in_first-class_cricket" title="Amateur status in first-class cricket">amateur</a> cricketer and later captain of England, noted that Rhodes was comparatively unsuccessful at the start of the year but came back well to take 193 wickets. Warner wrote that Rhodes at this time was accused of being easy to face on a wicket which suited the batsmen, although Warner himself did not agree.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_all-rounder_to_specialist_batsman">From all-rounder to specialist batsman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: From all-rounder to specialist batsman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Warner toured prolifically with cricket teams and was chosen to captain the first <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_Australia_in_1903%E2%80%9304" title="English cricket team in Australia in 1903–04">MCC-sponsored tour of Australia</a> in the winter of 1903–04. Warner was primarily responsible for the selection of players, and he selected Rhodes among his first choices for the team.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/K._S._Ranjitsinhji" class="mw-redirect" title="K. S. Ranjitsinhji">K. S. Ranjitsinhji</a> predicted that Rhodes "would not take a dozen wickets" on the tour,<sup id="cite_ref-w7_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w7-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Warner believed that Rhodes and Hirst were the best two bowlers in England. In the event, Warner rated Rhodes the "mainstay of the team",<sup id="cite_ref-w7_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w7-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and <i>Wisden</i> observed that he proved critics wrong, establishing himself as the most effective bowler on the tour. The <i>Wisden</i> summary of the tour pointed out that rain made an unusually high number of pitches, by Australian standards, helpful for Rhodes's style of bowling, but he bowled well on all types of pitches.<sup id="cite_ref-w03_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w03-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On the whole tour, the Yorkshire bowler took 65 first-class wickets at an average of 16.23,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> including 31 wickets at an average of 15.74 in the Test matches.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>England won the Test series 3–2 after winning the first, second and fourth games. In the first match Rhodes contributed 40 runs to a tenth wicket partnership of 130 with <a href="/wiki/R._E._Foster" title="R. E. Foster">R. E. Foster</a>, who scored 287, to assist the team in building a large lead. This was a Test record partnership for the tenth wicket, and remained so for 70 years; until 2014, it was a record for England's 10th wicket.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Victor_Trumper" title="Victor Trumper">Victor Trumper</a> led an Australian fightback, scoring 185 <a href="/wiki/Not_out" title="Not out">not out</a>, only Rhodes could slow his scoring in conditions which, according to Warner, were very good for batting.<sup id="cite_ref-w127_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w127-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Steady bowling through the innings brought Rhodes figures of five for 94;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Warner wrote: "what we should have done without Rhodes I do not know".<sup id="cite_ref-w127_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w127-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the second Test, badly affected by the weather, Rhodes had a match analysis of 15 wickets for 124 runs,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> the best <a href="/wiki/Bowling_analysis" title="Bowling analysis">bowling analysis</a> recorded in a match between England and Australia  until 1934 and the equal highest number of wickets taken in a match by a single player at that time (although other players had given away fewer runs).<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Rain made the pitch very difficult to bat on, but <i>Wisden</i> praised Rhodes and observed that  eight catches were dropped from his bowling.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> His eight for 68 in the second innings remained his best figures in Tests.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Australia won the third Test, but the decisive fourth Test was won by England and Rhodes contributed with bat and ball. In the first innings, while the crowd chanted in an attempt to distract him, he took four for 33 as the last five Australian wickets fell for 17 runs in favourable batting conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-Warner3T_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warner3T-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Later, Rhodes added 55 for the tenth wicket in the second innings with his captain.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> However, he was less effective as England lost the final Test.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rhodes believed that the 1903–04 tour was a turning point in his career as a bowler and that afterwards he was never the same. Part of the reason was a change in his bowling style. He had noticed that it was necessary for him to bowl faster in Australia to be effective, and on his return to England he continued with this faster style until the First World War.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes thought that another reason for his relative bowling decline was the development of his batting which took up much of his time.  His biographer, Sidney Rogerson, speculates that further deterioration may have been caused by the strain of regular bowling on his fingers and wrist, and his more robust, muscular frame in his mid-twenties. Rogerson believes that Rhodes was affected by the break-up of the successful Yorkshire team which had peaked between 1900 and 1902. More batting responsibility was placed on his shoulders, and he received less support in the field as the team personnel changed. Consequently, Rhodes scored more runs and moved further up the <a href="/wiki/Batting_order_(cricket)" title="Batting order (cricket)">batting order</a> after 1903, but his bowling gradually declined until the war.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1904_English_cricket_season" title="1904 English cricket season">1904</a>, Rhodes took 131 wickets, the fewest in a season of his career to date.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He scored 1,537 runs, including two hundreds (the second and third of his career) to complete his second double.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He generally batted at number six or seven in the batting order, but in two games he opened the batting.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/1905_English_cricket_season" title="1905 English cricket season">1905</a>, Yorkshire won the Championship; Rhodes again completed the double, with 1,581 runs, his two hundreds including a double hundred.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He took 182 wickets,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> but <i>Wisden</i> judged that he was not as dangerous a bowler on slow wickets as he had been.<sup id="cite_ref-Rogerson,_p73_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogerson,_p73-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes played in four of the five Tests against <a href="/wiki/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1905" title="Australian cricket team in England in 1905">Australia that year</a>. He scored 29 and 39 not out in the first Test,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> but in the second, suffered an injured finger which reduced his effectiveness and caused him to miss the next Test.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In the fourth Test, Rhodes took five wickets in the match, including three for 36 in the second innings.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> However, the England captain, Stanley Jackson, showed, in the words of <i>Wisden</i>, "a curious want of faith in Rhodes", even though he was bowling well.<sup id="cite_ref-t41905_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t41905-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> His fielding was singled out for praise as he took four catches, two of them regarded as brilliant.<sup id="cite_ref-t41905_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t41905-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> England eventually won the series 2–0; Rhodes contributed 146 runs, at an average of 48.66 and a top score of 39 not out,<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and ten wickets at an average of 31.40.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haigh,_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Three men in dark suits, two sitting on chairs and the third stood behind" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Haigh%2C_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg/220px-Haigh%2C_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Haigh%2C_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg/330px-Haigh%2C_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Haigh%2C_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg/440px-Haigh%2C_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="519" data-file-height="706" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haigh,_Hirst_and_Rhodes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>From left to right: <a href="/wiki/Schofield_Haigh" title="Schofield Haigh">Schofield Haigh</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Hirst" title="George Hirst">George Hirst</a> and Rhodes. The Yorkshire teammates at <a href="/wiki/Marsden,_West_Yorkshire" title="Marsden, West Yorkshire">Marsden</a>, 1905.</div></div></div>
<p>The relative deterioration in Rhodes's bowling continued into the <a href="/wiki/1906_English_cricket_season" title="1906 English cricket season">1906 season</a> when <i>Wisden</i> commented that he had lost his sharp spin and was not dangerous on a hard wicket.<sup id="cite_ref-Rogerson,_p73_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogerson,_p73-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes scored 1,721 runs,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> now regularly opening the batting, and completed another double with 128 wickets, but the <i>Wisden</i> correspondent did not believe this compensated for his lost bowling.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/1907_English_cricket_season" title="1907 English cricket season">1907</a>, Rhodes scored fewer runs and increased his bowling aggregate, securing 173 wickets in a wet season.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> <i>Wisden</i> believed his greater bowling success was due to a reduced batting contribution, but he still completed the double by scoring 1,045 runs.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> During that season, Rhodes was again asked to open the batting for Yorkshire and he was chosen as the permanent replacement for <a href="/wiki/John_Tunnicliffe" title="John Tunnicliffe">John Tunnicliffe</a> as Yorkshire's opening batsman. Several batsmen had been tried in the position,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> but Rhodes's superior defensive technique with the bat secured him the role.<sup id="cite_ref-H70_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H70-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Despite the increase in wickets, Rhodes was not picked for any of the Tests that year against <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_cricket_team" title="South Africa national cricket team">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colin_Blythe" title="Colin Blythe">Colin Blythe</a> being preferred.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rhodes and Blythe both went to Australia the following winter (1907–08) <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_Australia_in_1907%E2%80%9308" title="English cricket team in Australia in 1907–08">with MCC</a>, but Rhodes was now regarded primarily as a batsman and only a "change" bowler who would be the third or fourth used.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> In the five Test series, lost 4–1 by England, Rhodes scored 205 runs at an average of 20.50,<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> including his first Test fifty in the fourth innings of the last Test. He took four for 102 in Australia's second innings of that Test,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and finished the Test series with seven wickets at an average of 60.14.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In all first-class matches on the tour, Rhodes scored 929 runs at an average of 48.89<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and took 31 wickets at an average of 34.48.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He followed this with another double in <a href="/wiki/1908_English_cricket_season" title="1908 English cricket season">1908</a> of 1,660 runs and 106 wickets<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> as Yorkshire won the County Championship.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/1909_English_cricket_season" title="1909 English cricket season">1909</a>, Rhodes scored 2,094 runs at an average of 40.26, which was to remain his second highest run aggregate and average for an English cricket season,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and took 141 wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Sidney Rogerson believed that this season marked the completion of his transformation into a batsman.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> This view was supported by <i>Wisden</i>, which judged that he had "now become such an exceptionally good batsman that the regret one used to feel at his ever giving his mind to run getting has lost its force."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> He played in four of the five <a href="/wiki/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1909" title="Australian cricket team in England in 1909">Tests against Australia</a> in 1909;  his omission from the second Test was later described as an error of judgement by the editor of <i>Wisden</i>, one of many selectorial blunders as England lost the series two games to one.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes scored 168 runs at an average of 33.60,<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and took 11 wickets at an average of 22.00.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In the first Test, he had a quiet time, scoring an unbeaten 15, batting at number eight, and bowling only one over.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Recalled for the third Test, Rhodes bowled a spell in which four wickets were captured for seven runs, before being hit for four fours in one over by Trumper.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> His first innings figures were four for 38 and he took another two wickets for 44 runs in the second innings.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In the fourth Test, <i>Wisden</i> believed that Rhodes alone bowled well on the second day,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> taking five for 83. Although moved up the order to bat at number five, he scored just five runs in the match.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In the final Test, he batted at number three and scored two fifties, 66 and 54,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> adding 104 in the first innings with C. B. Fry and another 61 to save the game with the same batsman in the second.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_batsman">Opening batsman</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Opening batsman">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_batting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Before and after pictures of a cricketer hitting a ball" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rhodes_batting.jpg/220px-Rhodes_batting.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rhodes_batting.jpg/330px-Rhodes_batting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Rhodes_batting.jpg/440px-Rhodes_batting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1615" data-file-height="1161" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_batting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Before and after pictures of Rhodes playing a drive, photographed by George Beldam in 1906</div></div></div>
<p>In the 1909–10 English winter, <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_South_Africa_in_1909%E2%80%9310" title="English cricket team in South Africa in 1909–10">MCC toured South Africa</a> with a team below full Test strength. Rhodes opened the batting throughout the tour, partnering <a href="/wiki/Jack_Hobbs" title="Jack Hobbs">Jack Hobbs</a> for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> However, <i>Wisden</i> stated that only Hobbs would have been sure of his batting place in a full strength England team, and that both Rhodes and <a href="/wiki/David_Denton_(cricketer)" title="David Denton (cricketer)">David Denton</a>, the next best batsmen, were a long way behind Hobbs.<sup id="cite_ref-sa9_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sa9-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In all first-class matches, Rhodes scored 499 runs at an average of 26.26,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> with three fifties, and took 21 wickets at 25.47.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In the Test series, which South Africa won 3–2, Rhodes took only two wickets in the five games. As a batsman, however, he  shared some large partnerships with Hobbs. England lost the first two Tests, although in the first Rhodes and Hobbs put on 159 for the first wicket, of which Rhodes made 66.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In the second Test the pair put on 94 in the first innings and 48 in the second,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes made little impact on the third and fourth Tests;<sup id="cite_ref-statsguru_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statsguru-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> in the final Test, an England victory, he and Hobbs scored 221 together, Rhodes making what was then his highest Test score of 77.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>  <i>Wisden</i> stated that while overshadowed by the brilliance of Hobbs, Rhodes in this innings batted without mistakes.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  In the five Tests Rhodes scored 226 runs,  averaging 25.11.<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> During the tour Rhodes and Hobbs developed mutual trust while batting together, to the point where they could score runs without having to call to each other. This degree of understanding was unusual at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> After the Test series ended, several amateur members of the team wanted to extend the tour into <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/Professional_sports" title="Professional sports">professionals</a> refused to take part as their contracts did not cover this and they would have effectively played for no wages. Rhodes, although not the ring-leader, was influential in this strike, and a sports newspaper, <i>Winning Post</i>, singled him out as responsible in an article highly critical of him and the other professionals.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1910_English_cricket_season" title="1910 English cricket season">1910</a> domestic season Rhodes was less productive in batting and bowling, and Yorkshire finished only eighth in the County Championship, a result considered very poor within the county.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes scored 1,465 runs at an average of 26.63,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and took 88 wickets at an average of 18.98, the first time since the start of his career that he had taken less than 100 wickets in an English season.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/1911_English_cricket_season" title="1911 English cricket season">1911</a>, when Yorkshire finished seventh in the County Championship, it was a fine, dry summer, which meant generally good batting wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes was more productive with 2,261 runs, the second and final time that he  passed 2,000 runs in an English summer, and the highest season's total of his career. He averaged 38.32 with the bat,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and took 117 wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes was given a <a href="/wiki/Benefit_(sports)" title="Benefit (sports)">benefit match</a> against <a href="/wiki/Lancashire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Lancashire County Cricket Club">Lancashire</a> from which he received £750 (around £57,000 in 2010). After Yorkshire launched an appeal, the total was boosted to £2,200 (worth around £167,000 in 2010), still considerably less than the record benefit total of £3,703 raised for George Hirst in 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Measuringworth_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Measuringworth-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Batting_success_in_Australia">Batting success in Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Batting success in Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In September 1911 Rhodes made his third visit to Australia, this time as the opening partner of Jack Hobbs. The tour proved to be the "absolute pinnacle of his success as a batsman", according to Rogerson.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Under the captaincy of <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Douglas" title="Johnny Douglas">Johnny Douglas</a>, England won the <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_Australia_in_1911%E2%80%9312" title="English cricket team in Australia in 1911–12">1911–12 Test series</a> against Australia 4–1, after losing the first Test. While the success of the tourists was attributed to their powerful bowling attack, C. B. Fry described the English victories as "a succession of triumphs for Jack Hobbs and Rhodes as first wicket batsmen."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Pelham Warner, who was nominally captain but missed the entire series due to illness, said that in "innings after innings they [Hobbs and Rhodes] gave us a wonderful start", adding that he had run out of words to praise their contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-warner_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warner-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the first Test, the only one of the series in which he did not open, Rhodes made 41 and 0 in England's defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In the second match, opening with Hobbs, Rhodes scored 61 in the first innings, passing 1,000 Test career runs in the process.<sup id="cite_ref-2nd1911_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2nd1911-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <i>Wisden</i> recorded that apart from Rhodes and <a href="/wiki/J._W._Hearne" title="J. W. Hearne">J. W. Hearne</a>, with whom he shared a century partnership, the batting was very disappointing.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In the second innings, Rhodes added 57 for the first wicket with Hobbs, helping England to an eight-wicket victory.<sup id="cite_ref-2nd1911_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2nd1911-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> In the next Test Rhodes scored 59 out of an opening partnership of 147 with Hobbs, and 57 not out as England won again, this time by seven wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In the fourth Test, which England won overwhelmingly to take the series, Rhodes scored 179 as he and Hobbs scored 323 for the first wicket. At the time, this was a Test record partnership for any wicket. As of 2015, it remains England's highest first wicket partnership against Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> This was Rhodes's first Test century, and remained his highest Test score.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <i>Wisden</i> commented that  his seven-hour innings was "a remarkable display of careful batting."<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>  In the final Test victory Rhodes put on 76 with Hobbs in the second innings,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> to finish the series with 463 runs at an average of 57.87, the best series average of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> On the tour as a whole, he scored 1,098 runs at an average of 54.90,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> but he did not take a single first-class wicket;<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> in the Tests he only bowled 18 overs.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Triangular_tournament">Triangular tournament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Triangular tournament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CB_Fry_batting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A cricketer in his batting stance." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/CB_Fry_batting.jpg/220px-CB_Fry_batting.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="446" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/CB_Fry_batting.jpg/330px-CB_Fry_batting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/CB_Fry_batting.jpg/440px-CB_Fry_batting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="763" data-file-height="1546" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CB_Fry_batting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>C.B. Fry, pictured in 1906, was Rhodes's England captain in 1912.</div></div></div>
<p>On their return home for the <a href="/wiki/1912_English_cricket_season" title="1912 English cricket season">1912 season</a> England, captained by C. B. Fry, were involved in the first-ever <a href="/wiki/1912_Triangular_Tournament" title="1912 Triangular Tournament">triangular Test tournament</a>, consisting of matches between England, Australia and South Africa. This experiment was severely affected by wet weather, the weakness of the South African side, and a dispute among the Australian side which resulted in substandard team being sent.<sup id="cite_ref-1913notes_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1913notes-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes played as Hobbs' opening partner in each of England's six matches and once again won praise from <i>Wisden</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-1913notes_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1913notes-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> In England's first match, a victory against South Africa, Rhodes scored 36, his steady defence being described as invaluable.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> In the following drawn game against Australia, Hobbs and Rhodes scored 112 for the first wicket. Rhodes scored 59, his first 52 runs being scored out of a total of 77 before he slowed down; <i>Wisden</i> reported that the later part of his innings was "as cautious as the first part was brilliant".<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Later in the match Rhodes bowled and took three wickets for 59, his only bowling success of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After a quiet second match against South Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-triangle_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triangle-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes scored 92 out of a total of 203 in a rain-ruined game against Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>  The difficult batting conditions were such that Fry described Rhodes as "digging his runs out of the slush."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes had another poor match against South Africa,<sup id="cite_ref-triangle_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-triangle-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> but in the final match against Australia, which would decide the winner of the tournament, Rhodes scored 49 in an opening stand of 107 with Hobbs in the first innings, considered a great achievement in testing batting conditions. England went on to win in the match and hence the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes had scored 204 runs at an average of 51.00 against Australia, but only 53 runs at an average of 13.25 against the South Africans.<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In all first-class matches that summer, Rhodes scored 1,576 runs (averaging 30.90),<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and took 53 wickets (average 21.98), his lowest total of wickets in an English season, and only the second time since 1903 that he had not completed the double.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Last_pre-war_seasons">Last pre-war seasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Last pre-war seasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Rhodes again failed to complete the double in <a href="/wiki/1913_English_cricket_season" title="1913 English cricket season">1913</a>, scoring 1,963 runs (average 32.71) and taking 86 wickets (average 21.88).<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the 1913–14 English winter, Rhodes went to <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_South_Africa_in_1913%E2%80%9314" title="English cricket team in South Africa in 1913–14">South Africa with the MCC</a> under the captaincy of  Douglas. A strong England side won the five-match series 4–0 against weak opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-SA1913_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA1913-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes scored 731 runs in first-class matches, averaging 34.80,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and took 31 wickets at 21.35,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> which led Wisden to comment on his value as an all-rounder.<sup id="cite_ref-SA1913_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA1913-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In the second Test Rhodes took one wicket, his 100th in Test matches, and completed the double of 1,000 runs and 100 wickets in Tests; the first England player to do so, he was only the third player to reach the double after Australians <a href="/wiki/George_Giffen" title="George Giffen">George Giffen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monty_Noble" title="Monty Noble">Monty Noble</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In the same match, Rhodes made his second and final Test century, scoring 152 and adding 141 for the first wicket with <a href="/wiki/Albert_Relf" title="Albert Relf">Albert Relf</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> He batted for more than five hours, and <i>Wisden</i> said that he "was too cautious to please the crowd, but his steadiness was invaluable to his side."<sup id="cite_ref-t2sa_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t2sa-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> His batting was overshadowed, as <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Barnes" title="Sydney Barnes">Sydney Barnes</a> took 17 wickets in the match.<sup id="cite_ref-t2sa_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t2sa-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes resumed his opening partnership with Hobbs in the third Test, sharing a stand of 100,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> followed by opening partnerships of 92 and 133 in the fourth Test, the only drawn match of the series. In this match Rhodes took three wickets for 33 in the first South African innings.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> In all Tests on the tour Rhodes scored 289 runs at an average of 41.28<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and took six wickets (average 32.50).<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the final season before the First World War, Rhodes scored 1,377 runs. Yorkshire used him more often as a bowler and his tally of wickets consequently increased to 118, enabling him to complete another double.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Following the outbreak of war in August 1914, <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_Great_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Cricket in the Great War">first-class cricket came to an end for four years</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> While many cricketers joined the army  Rhodes, like George Hirst and Schofield Haigh, went to work in a munitions factory in Huddersfield. He and  Hirst were paid by Yorkshire to be available to play in war-time cricket matches on a certain number of Saturdays.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_after_the_First_World_War">Career after the First World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Career after the First World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leading_bowler_again">Leading bowler again</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Leading bowler again">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When cricket resumed after the war in <a href="/wiki/1919_English_cricket_season" title="1919 English cricket season">1919</a>, no-one was sure how popular county cricket would be and so the County Championship matches were reduced to two days instead of three. However, critics and players judged the experiment  a failure,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> owing to the long hours of play and frequent travelling which arose from playing up to three games a week; Rhodes and other players were also dissatisfied by wages offered.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Yorkshire won the championship with a much-changed side from that which had played in 1914. The bowling attack was weaker: Hirst's age lessened his effectiveness with the ball, <a href="/wiki/Major_Booth" title="Major Booth">Major Booth</a> was killed in the war, and <a href="/wiki/Alonzo_Drake" title="Alonzo Drake">Alonzo Drake</a> died from illness in January 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, Rhodes decided to make up the shortfall by resuming full-time bowling.<sup id="cite_ref-r121_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r121-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> With increased practice, he took more wickets and regained his confidence. Although unable to spin or flight the ball as well as previously, Rhodes bowled a very accurate length and used his great experience effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-r121_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r121-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>  The  success of <a href="/wiki/Percy_Holmes" title="Percy Holmes">Percy Holmes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Sutcliffe" title="Herbert Sutcliffe">Herbert Sutcliffe</a> as opening batsmen meant that, although Rhodes began the season opening the batting, he was able to move down the order and bat at number four.<sup id="cite_ref-r121_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r121-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> He scored 1,237 runs,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and by taking 164 wickets at an average of 14.42,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> finished top of the national first-class bowling averages.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Around this time, Rhodes was approached by <a href="/wiki/Haslingden_Cricket_Club" title="Haslingden Cricket Club">Haslingden Cricket Club</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Lancashire_League_(cricket)" title="Lancashire League (cricket)">Lancashire League</a>, to play cricket for them as a professional. Rhodes, primarily through unhappiness with the 1919 playing conditions, seriously considered the offer before he declined. Some of his concerns were addressed before the following season, when matches returned to three days and wages were increased.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/1920_English_cricket_season" title="1920 English cricket season">following season</a>, Rhodes scored 1,123 runs,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> took 161 wickets at an average of 13.18,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and was chosen to go to Australia with the <a href="/wiki/English_cricket_team_in_Australia_in_1920%E2%80%9321" title="English cricket team in Australia in 1920–21">1920–21 MCC touring team</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Australian_tour.2C_1920.E2.80.9321"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Australian_tour,_1920–21">Australian tour, 1920–21</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Australian tour, 1920–21">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff" class="image"><img alt="Two cricketers on a field" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="384" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_and_Waddington.tiff" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rhodes (left) and <a href="/wiki/Abe_Waddington" title="Abe Waddington">Abe Waddington</a> on tour in Australia in 1920</div></div></div>
<p>As English cricket had not fully recovered from the effects of the war,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> the team which toured Australia was weak in bowling. Confronted by a far better Australian side  than anyone had expected, England lost all five Test matches, an unprecedented result that <i>Wisden</i> regarded as a "disaster".<sup id="cite_ref-Wisden20/21_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wisden20/21-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes now played for Yorkshire as a middle-order batsman and front-line bowler but England's captain Douglas showed uncertainty whether to use Rhodes in this capacity, or to revert to his pre-war role as Hobbs's opening partner.<sup id="cite_ref-r130_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r130-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Until the first Test Rhodes batted mainly down the order; after this he returned to opening the batting. On the tour Rhodes scored two centuries, one a double-century, totalling in all 730 runs in all first-class matches at an average of 38.42.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-r130_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r130-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Although a leading bowler in England in 1919 and 1920, Rhodes bowled infrequently and with limited success.<sup id="cite_ref-r130_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r130-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> After taking six for 39 against Victoria in helpful conditions,<sup id="cite_ref-t150_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t150-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> he rarely bowled,<sup id="cite_ref-r130_132-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r130-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> and took only 18 first-class wickets (averaging 26.61) on the tour.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Tests, Rhodes scored 238 runs at an average of 23.80, with a highest score of 73 in the fourth Test.<sup id="cite_ref-testbatting_60-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbatting-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In the first Test, a score of 45 took him past 2,000 Test runs.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> As a bowler, Rhodes took four Test wickets in the series at an average of 61.25; his best figures were three for 61 in the third Test.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes later said that Douglas was reluctant to use him, believing his bowling would be ineffective on Australian pitches.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> <i>Wisden</i> commented: "It must be said, however, that in a summer of continuous sunshine&#160;– remarkable even for Australia&#160;– the bowlers received no help."<sup id="cite_ref-Wisden20/21_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wisden20/21-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, much of Rhodes's tour, according to <a href="/wiki/A._A._Thomson" title="A. A. Thomson">A. A. Thomson</a>, "may be fairly regarded as failure."<sup id="cite_ref-t150_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t150-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Tour manager and Yorkshire secretary <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Toone" title="Frederick Toone">Frederick Toone</a>, with whom Rhodes had already had a disagreement during the 1920 season, apparently said that "Wilfred's finished", a remark later reported to Rhodes.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior_professional">Senior professional</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Senior professional">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1921_English_cricket_season" title="1921 English cricket season">1921 season</a> was a turning point for Rhodes for several reasons. His regular England career ended during the visit of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1921" title="Australian cricket team in England in 1921">Australians</a>. The tourists, as <i>Wisden</i> reported, overwhelmed England, exposing many weaknesses in the team, and reduced the English selectors to "catch[ing] at straws".<sup id="cite_ref-1922w_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1922w-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> 30 players were used in the five-match Test series, which England lost by three matches to none.<sup id="cite_ref-1922w_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1922w-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes played in the first Test, scored 19 and 10 and took two wickets in a heavy defeat. Although his performance was no worse than that of others, he was dropped from the team for the rest of the series and did not play another Test for five years.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> At the time, it was suggested his place was lost because he was uncomfortable against the <a href="/wiki/Fast_bowling" class="mw-redirect" title="Fast bowling">fast bowling</a> of <a href="/wiki/Jack_Gregory_(cricketer)" title="Jack Gregory (cricketer)">Jack Gregory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ted_McDonald" title="Ted McDonald">Ted McDonald</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> who devastated and demoralised many English batsmen during the season.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> As a result of these problems with pace bowling Rhodes altered his <a href="/wiki/Batting_(cricket)#Stance" title="Batting (cricket)">batting stance</a> to  use the "two-eyed stance"; instead of using the traditional technique of standing at right angles to the bowler, the batsman turned his body towards the bowler. Critics complained that this method was ugly; it restricted the shots that could be made, and led to some batsmen using their pads  as an extra form of defence to stop the ball hitting the wicket.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> According to his <i>Wisden</i> obituary, Rhodes was one of the first men to adopt this batting stance.<sup id="cite_ref-obituary_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes faced a further development following the retirements of Hirst and Denton from Yorkshire; he became the county's senior professional. This position offered no official powers or responsibilities but was nevertheless significant as senior professionals influenced tactics, strategy and morale. Rhodes held this post until his retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In all first-class cricket in 1921, Rhodes scored 1,474 runs at an average of 39.83.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> This included his highest first-class score of 267 not out against <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire_County_Cricket_Club" title="Leicestershire County Cricket Club">Leicestershire</a>, struck on the day England began the second Test, having just dropped Rhodes.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes took 141 wickets in the season, at an average of 13.27.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In the autumn, he travelled to India, coaching and playing for the <a href="/wiki/Bhupinder_Singh_of_Patiala" title="Bhupinder Singh of Patiala">Maharaja of Patiala</a>'s private team; Rhodes repeated this trip every year until 1927, sometimes accompanied by other players. On five occasions in India he completed a 1,000 runs and 100 wickets double, although most of these games were not first-class.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In each of the four seasons from 1922 to 1925, Yorkshire won the County Championship. Rhodes scored over 1,000 runs each year, averaging over 30 except in 1924; in 1925 his average was 40.91, only the second time it exceeded 40 in an English cricket season.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes, by now part of a very powerful county bowling attack, was usually the fourth or fifth bowler used.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Although he imparted less spin to the ball than in his younger days, he continually bowled a good length and placed fielders in positions which very effectively blocked the scoring opportunities of the batsmen.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> He took over 100 wickets in 1922, 1923 and 1924, but took only 57 in 1925,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> a very good year for batting.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> As Yorkshire's senior professional Rhodes was very influential in this period. He cultivated a hostile attitude among the bowlers, directed the team tactically and raised its standard of fielding.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Alan Hill wrote that Yorkshire captains (who were usually poor cricketers) generally deferred to Rhodes as senior professional; for example, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Lupton" title="Arthur Lupton">Arthur Lupton</a>, captain from 1925 to 1927, "very wisely left the cricket affairs to the joint supervision of Rhodes and <a href="/wiki/Emmott_Robinson" title="Emmott Robinson">Emmott Robinson</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-h107_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-h107-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Stories emerged that he was an "overmighty subject", arranging the positions of fielders and changing the bowler without reference to his nominal captain.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In one story, Yorkshire had scored around 400. Lupton, hoping to score some easy runs, came out of the amateur dressing room with his bat when a young professional touched his arm and said, "It's all right, sir.
