Mr Rhodes has <a href="/wiki/Declaration_and_forfeiture" title="Declaration and forfeiture">declared</a> [the innings over]."<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> However, all the captains to whom biographer Sidney Rogerson spoke mentioned their good relations with Rhodes, although they agreed that he could be difficult.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Beverley_Lyon" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverley Lyon">Beverley Lyon</a>, who captained Gloucestershire between 1929 and 1934, criticised Rhodes for insisting young professionals take the game seriously, thus promoting a no-risk attitude.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recalled_for_the_Oval">Recalled for the Oval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Recalled for the Oval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A three tiered Victorian red-brick building with flags flying on the roof and a clock at the top. There are large numbers of spectators watching a cricket match." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg/220px-The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg/330px-The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg/440px-The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2730" data-file-height="2122" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Oval_Pavilion.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Pavilion at the Oval, the scene of Rhodes successes in 1902 and 1926. Although this is a modern picture, the pavilion is the same as it was when Rhodes played there.</div></div></div><p>Reviewing the 1925 season, <i>Wisden</i> commented on Rhodes's age and reduced performance. "In the nature of things, Rhodes, approaching the completion of his 48th year, could not be expected to prove very deadly in a dry summer&#160;... If less effective in bowling, he did fine work with the bat".<sup id="cite_ref-r142_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r142-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> However, in <a href="/wiki/1926_English_cricket_season" title="1926 English cricket season">1926</a>, <i>Wisden</i> reported that, despite his age and in contrast to the other bowlers in the team, Rhodes "came out in wonderful form&#160;... [His] triumph delighted everybody&#160;... He not only accomplished skilful work in bowling but made his thousand runs [in county matches] with an average of 40."<sup id="cite_ref-r142_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r142-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes doubled his wicket tally from 1925, taking 115 at an average of 14.86.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In all first-class matches he scored 1,132 runs  (average 34.30), the final time he passed 1,000 runs in a season, and completed his 16th and final double.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1926 <a href="/wiki/Australian_cricket_team_in_England_in_1926" title="Australian cricket team in England in 1926">the Australians toured England</a> for the first time since 1921. The English selectors decided to add two professional cricketers to their committee, choosing Rhodes and Jack Hobbs.<sup id="cite_ref-r143_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r143-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> With Rhodes in such good form and leading the bowling averages, the selectors tried to convince him to play for England on several occasions through the season but he refused on the grounds that younger men should be chosen.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The first four Tests were all drawn; the selectors were conscious, as England entered the final Test, the team had won only one of its previous 19 matches against Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-r143_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r143-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>  The deciding game, at the Oval, was to be played to a finish no matter how long it took.<sup id="cite_ref-oval26_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oval26-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The selectors dropped the captain, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Carr_(cricketer)" title="Arthur Carr (cricketer)">Arthur Carr</a>, and replaced him with the inexperienced <a href="/wiki/Percy_Chapman" title="Percy Chapman">Percy Chapman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> They also recalled Rhodes, aged nearly 49, having finally overcome his objections.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> According to <i>Wisden</i>, the selection of Rhodes "naturally occasioned a good deal of surprise".<sup id="cite_ref-oval26_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oval26-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>England batted first, but made a disappointing total of 280;<sup id="cite_ref-oval26_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oval26-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes, batting at number seven, scored 28.<sup id="cite_ref-Ovalscore_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ovalscore-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In the Australian innings of 302 Rhodes bowled 25 overs and took two wickets for 35, helped by a worn area on the pitch which helped him to spin the ball.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> He later described feeling nervous when first bowling, but said that he was heartened by the warm welcome he received from the crowd.<sup id="cite_ref-Ovalscore_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ovalscore-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> After the start of England's second innings an overnight thunderstorm soaked the pitch, leaving it very difficult to bat on next day. However,  Hobbs and Sutcliffe put on 172 runs for the first wicket and England eventually scored 436, leaving Australia to make 415 to win in unfavourable conditions for batting.<sup id="cite_ref-oval26_160-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oval26-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes quickly began taking wickets, and went on to take four for 44.<sup id="cite_ref-Ovalscore_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ovalscore-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Australia were bowled out for 125, and amid widespread jubilation, England won the series and  Ashes. <i>Wisden's</i> judged Rhodes's selection to be "crowned with complete success", his bowling  "proving no small factor in determining the issue of the struggle."<sup id="cite_ref-oval26_160-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oval26-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Wisden</i> editor believed Rhodes had shown himself still to be England's best bowler and called his triumph  "immensely popular."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_career">Late career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Late career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_captaincy_affair_of_1927" title="Yorkshire captaincy affair of 1927">Yorkshire captaincy affair of 1927</a></div>
<p>Rhodes continued to play for Yorkshire until 1930, but averaged under 30 with the bat in each season and only scored one more hundred, in 1928. He failed to reach 1,000 runs in  a season again,<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> but as a bowler he took 85 wickets in 1927, 115  in 1928 and 100  in 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1927 the Yorkshire committee opened a public testimonial for Rhodes, donating £250 themselves; it eventually raised £1,821,<sup id="cite_ref-r149_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r149-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> worth more than £80,000 in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Measuringworth_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Measuringworth-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> During the 1927 season, he played his 1,000th first-class match when Yorkshire played Nottinghamshire on 23 July, becoming the first and, as of 2015, only cricketer to play so many first-class matches.<sup id="cite_ref-o_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-o-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> On 10 May 1929, he became the first man to take 4,000 first-class wickets during a match against <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Cricket_Club" title="Oxford University Cricket Club">Oxford University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> As of 2015, no other player has taken so many wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-wickets_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wickets-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1927, Yorkshire wished to <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_captaincy_affair_of_1927" title="Yorkshire captaincy affair of 1927">appoint a more competent and permanent captain</a>, instead of continuing the succession of ineffective amateurs, and planned to ask Herbert Sutcliffe, a professional, to take the post. Frederick Toone encouraged Rhodes to offer his resignation as senior professional, possibly with a view to installing a new regime, but Rhodes declined.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the proposed appointment of Sutcliffe caused controversy; some members of the county believed Rhodes should be appointed. Rhodes pointed out he had not been offered the captaincy, nor had his views been sought. He felt unappreciated when he was not offered first refusal of the captaincy. A poll of Yorkshire members showed a marked preference for Rhodes over Sutcliffe as captain; the disagreements persuaded Sutcliffe to decline the offer, and another amateur was appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1929–30, Rhodes was selected in a MCC team, containing several veteran players,  to tour West Indies—Rhodes described it as an "old crocks" team. Given a heavy workload with the ball,<sup id="cite_ref-r149_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-r149-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>  he took 39 first-class wickets, averaging 24.28,<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and scored 129 runs at an average of 25.80 with a top score 36.<sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the four Test matches Rhodes took ten wickets at an average of 45.30.<sup id="cite_ref-testbowling_41-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-testbowling-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On 12 April 1930, the last day of the final Test, Rhodes was 52 years, 165 days, making him the oldest ever Test cricketer; this remains a record in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement_and_coaching">Retirement and coaching</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Retirement and coaching">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/1930_English_cricket_season" title="1930 English cricket season">1930 season</a>, Rhodes announced his intention to retire from cricket at the end of the summer. He was finding it harder to take wickets, and the workload placed on him in the West Indies had  decreased his enthusiasm for the game. By this time, <a href="/wiki/Hedley_Verity" title="Hedley Verity">Hedley Verity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bowes" title="Bill Bowes">Bill Bowes</a> had emerged to strengthen the Yorkshire bowling. Through an ex-captain of Yorkshire, <a href="/wiki/Harrow_School" title="Harrow School">Harrow School</a> offered Rhodes the post of  professional cricket coach, which he accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes missed several matches towards the end of the 1930 season, before ending his career at the <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_Festival" title="Scarborough Festival">Scarborough Festival</a>. His last match was for <a href="/wiki/H._D._G._Leveson_Gower" title="H. D. G. Leveson Gower">H. D. G. Leveson Gower</a>'s XI against the Australians, where his figures were five for 93;<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> he took a wicket with his last ball in first-class cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes's figures for his final season were 73 wickets at an average of 19.10 and 478 runs at an average of 22.76.<sup id="cite_ref-bowlingseasonbyseason_15-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bowlingseasonbyseason-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-batting_16-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-batting-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over his career Rhodes appeared in 1,110 first-class matches, which remains a world record in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In these games he scored 39,969 runs, the 17th highest career total of any batsman.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> He took 4,204 wickets, as of 2015 still the highest total in first-class cricket.<sup id="cite_ref-wickets_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wickets-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In his 58 Tests Rhodes scored 2,325 runs (average 30.19) and took 127 wickets (average 26.96).<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>  He was the first player in the world to accumulate 2,000 runs and 100 wickets in Tests.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rhodes coached at Harrow School until 1936. Cricket was very important to the school, and they were following the lead of <a href="/wiki/Eton_College" title="Eton College">Eton College</a> who had appointed George Hirst as their coach. However, Rhodes's personality and generally critical nature did not communicate well with privileged schoolboys who were accustomed to getting their own way, and he was eventually replaced with the more genial and sympathetic Middlesex professional <a href="/wiki/Patsy_Hendren" title="Patsy Hendren">Patsy Hendren</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Swanton,_p15_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swanton,_p15-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> This was in contrast to the success Hirst enjoyed at Eton.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> According to Bowes, Rhodes had vast technical knowledge, but unlike Hirst did not know how to get the best out of people. "[He] could not relate to beginners. But if you were a Test match player looking to get advice, Wilfred was superb."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_and_personality">Style and personality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Style and personality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A cricketer bowling, seen from the side" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg/220px-Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg/330px-Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg/440px-Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg 2x" data-file-width="992" data-file-height="1210" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhodes_bowling_side.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rhodes bowling, photographed by George Beldam in 1906.</div></div></div>
<p>As a bowler, Rhodes was recognised by critics as one of the greatest slow bowlers of all time. Very effective at dismissing batsmen on difficult pitches, it was difficult to score runs from his bowling even on a good batting surface. He could make the ball turn if the pitch offered the slightest assistance, particularly if it had been <a href="/wiki/Sticky_wicket" title="Sticky wicket">affected by rain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-W183_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W183-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Cricket writer <a href="/wiki/E._W._Swanton" title="E. W. Swanton">E. W. Swanton</a> described how Rhodes had "a beautifully controlled, economical and rhythmical action which ensured supreme accuracy of length and direction. He was a master of the stock left-hander's spin and could vary it with the ball that came on with the arm."<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>  In his early years as a bowler, Rhodes was able to spin the ball very sharply,<sup id="cite_ref-Rogerson,_p._62_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogerson,_p._62-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and while this ability decreased in later years, he became expert at working out a batsman's weaknesses.<sup id="cite_ref-Swanton,_p15_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swanton,_p15-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Critics considered him expert at flighting the ball; Neville Cardus wrote that "Flight was his secret. Flight and the curving line, now higher, now lower, tempting, inimical; every ball like every other ball, yet somehow unlike; each over in collusion with the others, part of a plot&#160;..."<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> In the early part of his career, his bowling partnership with Hirst, who shared Rhodes's Kirkheaton birthplace, was particularly effective and established a formidable reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> As time passed, his accuracy increased to the extent that it seemed every ball landed in exactly the same place.<sup id="cite_ref-H72_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H72-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In his first five seasons, he was top of the national bowling averages twice and in second place three times, while in the first six seasons after the war, he was first four times and second once. In his whole career, he only fell outside the top 20 in the bowling averages in four seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-H70_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H70-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rhodes claimed that he preferred batting to bowling.<sup id="cite_ref-s14_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s14-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> A right-handed batsman with a good defensive technique, Rhodes was a strong driver of the ball who scored more quickly in the earlier part of his career. Analysts maintained that Rhodes had only two or three effective shots, though his technique was good.<sup id="cite_ref-W183_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W183-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-H72_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H72-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Cricket writer <a href="/wiki/E._W._Swanton" title="E. W. Swanton">E. W. Swanton</a> described Rhodes as a "craftsman rather than an artist".<sup id="cite_ref-s14_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s14-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Neville Cardus, in his obituary of Rhodes, said that the Yorkshireman "made himself into a batsman by practice and hard thinking", and that while often "dour and parsimonious", he was capable  of hitting out.<sup id="cite_ref-obituary_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> After changing to the two-eyed stance more of his runs came on the leg-side;<sup id="cite_ref-s14_189-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s14-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> in later years, Rhodes often used his <a href="/wiki/Pads" title="Pads">pads</a> rather than play a shot, a tactic generally regarded as negative.<sup id="cite_ref-H72_188-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H72-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> A feature of his batting career was his successful opening partnership with Hobbs, particularly their enterprise in running between the wickets.<sup id="cite_ref-s14_189-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-s14-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> In his career, he scored over 190 in an innings five times and twice scored centuries in each innings of a match.<sup id="cite_ref-H70_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H70-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Although Rhodes's primary function varied between bowler and batsman, he recorded 16 doubles to establish a record for any cricketer.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When Rhodes was involved in matches, Cardus believed that "he was not a man given to affability", showing annoyance on the field and being critical of the performances of others.<sup id="cite_ref-obituary_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> According to historian Anthony Woodhouse, Rhodes was a "dour, methodical and calculating cricketer."<sup id="cite_ref-W183_184-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W183-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Not popular in the way that a player like Hirst was popular, Rhodes "commanded respect rather than plaudits" in the words of Bowes.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> An introvert, he did not always get along with the more extrovert Hirst, possibly owing to mutual jealousy and some of Hirst's jocular comments, and was rarely pictured smiling.<sup id="cite_ref-H70_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H70-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> However, Rhodes became more relaxed and approachable in later life, particularly after his eyesight failed.<sup id="cite_ref-W183_184-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W183-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Cardus was surprised, after meeting him in 1950, at how much more readily Rhodes engaged in conversation, commenting that "history comes from his mouth in rivers".<sup id="cite_ref-H72_188-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H72-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> His obituary in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> concluded: "Gruff or mellow, he was all of a piece, a fighting Yorkshireman, superbly gifted."<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wilfred_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In October 1899, Rhodes, aged 22, married Sarah Elizabeth Stancliffe, who lived in Kirkheaton and was two years his senior. They lived in a farmhouse, shared with other people, at Bog Hall near Kirkheaton.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> On 25 August 1902 his wife gave birth to a daughter, their only child.<sup id="cite_ref-Rogerson,_p63_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rogerson,_p63-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes found Yorkshire's dealings with money to be ungenerous;<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> following his benefit in 1911 Yorkshire, as was their custom, paid only one-third of the money to Rhodes and kept back the rest to invest on his behalf, only paying out the interest. Rhodes considered this to be unfair; however, he was able to use the money to build a stone house at <a href="/wiki/Marsh,_Huddersfield" title="Marsh, Huddersfield">Marsh, Huddersfield</a>, which his family moved into in the autumn of 1912. He lived there until 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From around 1936 Rhodes's sight began to fail, and on the outbreak of war in 1939 he was unable to take up a wartime job.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Eventually a specialist diagnosed <a href="/wiki/Glaucoma" title="Glaucoma">glaucoma</a>, but at that stage nothing could be done.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Rhodes was still able to see well enough to watch cricket and play golf, although by 1946 he was unable to read a newspaper. Another specialist was consulted in 1951 and an operation performed, but by 1952 Rhodes was completely blind. The build-up of pain led  to the removal of his left eyeball in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> In 1950, Sarah Rhodes suffered a heart attack, which limited the help she could give to her husband; in 1954 she died a few months before her 80th birthday. Rhodes then sold his house at Marsh and moved in with his daughter and her husband, with whom he later moved to Bournemouth.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> He continued to attend cricket matches where he was able to follow the play despite his blindness,<sup id="cite_ref-obituary_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and was frequently sought out by cricketers and asked for his advice or opinion. Rhodes was given honorary life membership of Yorkshire in 1946, and of the MCC in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> When given membership of the MCC, along with other old professionals, Rhodes reacted characteristically; rather than showing pleasure, he responded, "I don't rightly know what it means yet."<sup id="cite_ref-H72_188-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H72-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> He died in 1973, aged 95.<sup id="cite_ref-obituary_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obituary-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, Rhodes was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Cricket_Hall_of_Fame" title="ICC Cricket Hall of Fame">ICC Cricket Hall of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
